<div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=132876912 id=\"132876912\" class=\"abstract-title\" >ABSTRACT</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Quadruply lensed quasars are extremely rare objects, but incredibly powerful cosmological tools. Only few dozen are known in the whole sky. Here we present the spectroscopic confirmation of two new quadruplets WG0214-2105 and WG2100-4452 discovered by Agnello\u00a0&amp; Spiniello (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) within the Dark Energy Survey public footprints. We have conducted spectroscopic follow-up of these systems with the Southern African Large Telescope as part of a program that aims at confirming the largest possible number of strong gravitational lenses in the equatorial and Southern hemisphere. For both systems, we present the sources spectra that allowed us to estimate their redshifts and unambiguously confirm their lensing nature. For the brighter deflector (WG2100-4452) we measure the spectroscopic redshift and the stellar velocity dispersion from optical absorption lines in the spectrum. For the other system we infer the lens redshift from photometry, being the quality of the spectra not good enough. We obtain photometry for both lenses, directly from multiband images, isolating the lenses from the quasars. One of the quadruplets, WG0214-2105, was also observed by Pan-STARRS, allowing us to estimate the apparent brightness of each quasar image at two different epochs, and thus to find evidence for flux variability. This result could suggest a microlensing event for the faintest components, although intrinsic variability cannot be excluded with only two epochs. Finally, we present simple lens models for both quadruplets, obtaining Einstein radii, singular isothermal ellipsoid velocity dispersions, ellipticities, and position angles of the lenses, as well as time-delay predictions assuming a concordance cosmological model.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;techniques: spectroscopic&quot;\">techniques: spectroscopic</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"surveys\">surveys</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: formation&quot;\">galaxies: formation</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=132876914 id=\"132876914\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">According to the estimate of Oguri\u00a0&amp; Marshall (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib45\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib45\" data-open=\"bib45\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>), quadruplets represent <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\sim }14{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|</span> of a statistically complete sample of lensed quasars. The quadruplet configuration, in fact, requires a closer alignment between the source and the deflector than the one needed for the more common doublet configuration.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">1</a></sup> However, when the number of source images is doubled, the information that can be gathered in terms of stellar mass fraction and deflector potential is larger (e.g. Schechter\u00a0&amp; Wambsganss <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib59\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib59\" data-open=\"bib59\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Treu\u00a0&amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib75\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib75\" data-open=\"bib75\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). Quadruplets have also been shown to be valuable cosmological tools (Refsdal <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib54\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib54\" data-open=\"bib54\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1964</a>; Blandford\u00a0&amp; Narayan <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1992</a>; Witt, Mao\u00a0&amp; Keeton <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib79\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib79\" data-open=\"bib79\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>; Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib70\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib70\" data-open=\"bib70\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Treu\u00a0&amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib75\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib75\" data-open=\"bib75\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Bonvin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) and useful for microlensing studies to investigate the inner parts of quasar accretion discs (Schechter\u00a0&amp; Wambsganss <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib57\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib57\" data-open=\"bib57\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Eigenbrod et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Blackburne et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Mediavilla et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Vernardos <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib78\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib78\" data-open=\"bib78\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). For instance, studies based on blind analysis have shown that a single quadruplet can be used to measure the so-called time-delay distance (<em>D</em><sub>\u0394<em>t</em></sub>), a multiplicative combination of the three angular diameter distances between the observer, deflector, and source,<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">2</a></sup> with an uncertainty of 5\u20137\u00a0per\u2009cent (Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib69\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib69\" data-open=\"bib69\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). Since <em>D</em><sub>\u0394<em>t</em></sub> is inversely proportional to the Hubble constant, <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> (Linder <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib69\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib69\" data-open=\"bib69\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), and more weakly dependent on other cosmological parameters, obtaining a precise estimation of it through time-delay lenses allows one to break some of the main degeneracies in the interpretation of cosmic microwave background data. Moreover, time-delay distances are independent of the local distance ladder and give comparable precision on <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>, providing a crucial test of potential systematic uncertainties.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn3\" data-open=\"fn3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">3</a></sup></p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper, we report the spectroscopic confirmation of two recently discovered quadruplets: WG0214-2105 and WG2100-4452, both identified in the Dark Energy Survey (DES; Abbott et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) DR1 public footprints, using the source-based methods developed and presented in Agnello\u00a0&amp; Spiniello (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, hereafter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>) to find lens candidates in wide-sky photometric multiband surveys. The spectroscopic confirmation has been carried out using the Southern African Large Telescope (SALT; Buckley, Swart\u00a0&amp; Meiring <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>) as part of the observing programme <em>Gotta catch\u2019em all</em> (2018-2-SCI-020, PI: Marchetti).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The paper is organized as follow. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>, we give details on the SALT observing programme and the selected candidates. A brief description of the two new quadruplets, including their coordinates and infrared magnitudes used at the pre-selection stage, is provided in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>, we report the results of a photometric analysis, which then leads to a preliminary variability analysis for one of the systems. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>, we present the obtained SALT spectra for both systems, and highlight the redshift determinations for the sources and the deflectors. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">6</a>, we provide simple lensing models for both quadruplets. We summarize our findings and conclude in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7\"></span><a href=\"#sec7\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">7</a>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Throughout the paper, we adopt a flat \u039b cold dark matter cosmology with \u03a9<sub>M</sub>\u00a0= 0.3, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0= 0.7, and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0= 70 kms<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=132876919 id=\"132876919\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 THE SALT OBSERVING PROGRAMME</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Our observing programme: \u2018<em>Gotta catch\u2019em All</em>, the spectroscopic follow-up of strong gravitational lenses from KiDS and KABS surveys\u2019 (PI: L. Marchetti, ID: 2018-2-SCI-020) has the goal of spectroscopically confirming optically selected strong gravitational lens (SL) candidates, both quasi-stellar object (QSO)\u2013galaxy, and galaxy\u2013galaxy (gravitational arcs) systems. The candidates have been found by exploiting the improved image quality and the more extended and homogeneous sky coverage achieved with new, deep optical surveys. In particular, we focus on the Kilo Degree Survey (KiDS; de Jong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), because of its depth, exquisite image quality and quite stringent seeing constraints [limiting magnitude of 25 at 5\u03c3 in 2 arcsec aperture and mean full width at half-maximum (FWHM) of 0.7 arcsec in <em>r</em> band], and on the KiDS VST-ATLAS Bridging Survey (KABS; Getman et\u00a0al. in preparation),<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn4\" data-open=\"fn4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">4</a></sup> which images a previously almost uncovered region of the southern sky. Finally, we also include a few very promising candidates from the DES public footprint, which were recently found by our team (Agnello\u00a0&amp; Spiniello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">After almost 2 yr, we have collected a list of \u223c300 high-grade candidates which need spectroscopic confirmation and redshift measurements to translate our lens model results (e.g. Einstein radii) into physical mass measurements. We have already presented the search methods as well as the KiDS candidates in recently published papers (Petrillo et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib51\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib51\" data-open=\"bib51\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib53\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib53\" data-open=\"bib53\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; Spiniello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, hereafter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a>), and we will present the KABS candidates in a paper in preparation (Spiniello et\u00a0al. in prep).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Full results from the first semester of SALT observations, still on-going, will be presented in a dedicated, future, paper (Marchetti et\u00a0al. in prep). In this paper, we focus on the DES candidates: two quadruply lensed QSOs for which the spectroscopic confirmation was the last required step to unambiguously confirm their lensing nature. These pilot observations have been carried out to test our strategy and integration times before proceeding with a larger candidate list (arcs and QSOs) from the KIDS and KABS surveys.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=132876923 id=\"132876923\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 TWO NEW QUADRUPLETS IN THE SOUTHERN HEMISPHERE: WG0214-2105 AND WG2100-4452</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Agnello (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, hereafter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">ARN18</a>) reported the discovery of WG0214-2105 (RAJ2000: 02:14:16.37, DECJ2000: -21:05:35.3), which was found by cross-matching the publicly available data of three wide-area sky surveys in the Southern hemisphere (DES DR1, Abbott et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; VST-ATLAS, Shanks et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; and Pan-STARRS, Chambers et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). The multiple images, in the typical fold/cross configurations, are characterized by \u2018white\u2019 optical colours, \u2018blue\u2019 mid-IR colours and high UV deficit (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">ARN18</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The discovery of WG2100-4452 (RA J2000: 21:00:14.9, Dec. J2000: \u221244:52:06.4) has been reported in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>, where we exploit several complementary methods to search for lensed quasars in wide-area photometric surveys. In particular, this previously unknown quadruplet in the DES footprint has been found by pre-selecting QSO-like objects based on infrared colours (from the Wide-Infrared Survey Explorer, WISE; Wright et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib80\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib80\" data-open=\"bib80\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) and then making use of the high spatial resolution of the Gaia Mission (Gaia Collaboration <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Lindegren et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) to identify single WISE objects with multiple Gaia matches. We refer the reader to <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> for a more comprehensive description of this and the other methods, and for a complete list of other similarly identified lens candidates.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Both WG0214-2105 and WG2100-4452 have also been shown to be easily compatible with simple lens models (Wynne\u00a0&amp; Schechter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib81\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib81\" data-open=\"bib81\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper we present their spectroscopic confirmation, with estimation of the source and deflector redshifts, as well as <em>griz</em>-photometry obtained directly from the DES images and lensing modelling. We note that a very recent paper, contemporary to this work, has been published by Lee (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>), reporting a spectroscopic confirmation of WG0214-2105 with Gemini Multi-Object Spectrographs. Here we provide a more detailed analysis of the spectral, photometric, and lensing properties of the latter system, comparing our inferences for the source and deflector redshifts with the related findings in Lee (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> reports, for the two lens systems, coordinates and WISE infrared magnitudes, used for pre-selection and converted from their native Vega system to AB, to better compare them with the optical ones given in the latter system throughout this paper. We also give details about the observational blocks (slit position, orientation, and integration times) that we will present in detail in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"132876929\" scrollto-destination=\"132876929\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Coordinates, infrared magnitudes from the WISE catalogue (Wright et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib80\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib80\" data-open=\"bib80\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>), converted in AB system and spectroscopic observations settings for the two quadruplets. For WG0214-2105 we obtained two different observation blocks, with two different position angle orientations (\u221235\u00b0 and +50\u00b0, respectively), as indicated in the table.</p></div> class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/132876929\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=132876930 id=\"132876930\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 ACCURATE ASTROMETRY AND PSF PHOTOMETRY ANALYSIS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Following the recipe detailed in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a>, we performed direct image analysis (DIA) on the multiband DES images of the two systems. Briefly, we simultaneously fitted a point-PSF (point spread function) model to all the QSO multiple images in each of the single-band cut-outs, for <em>griz</em> bands, and then generated subtracted images that we visually inspected to identify the position of the deflector. Accurate astrometry is, in fact, of great help when extracting the 1D spectra from the long-slit data and it is also very useful when performing lensing and mass modelling.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We then derived, for each band, photometry on all the components (A = brightest QSO image, D = faintest QSO image, G \u00a0=\u00a0lens galaxy) using the code <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). We calculated the PSF from a nearby star, to minimize the effect of distortion on the field and then modelled each quasar image simultaneously with a point-like PSF profile and the galaxy with a Se\u0155sic profile convolved with the PSF. Specifically, we assumed a de Vaucouleurs profile using a fixed Se\u0155sic index<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn5\" data-open=\"fn5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">5</a></sup><em>n</em>\u00a0=\u00a04, to model the light distribution of the lens galaxy.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> shows the results of the PSF fitting. For WG0214-2105, we also performed DIA on the Pan-STARRS images. In each line of the figure, the left-most panel shows the <em>griz</em>-combined colour cut-outs of 10 arcsec\u00a0\u00d7 10 arcsec size, and the middle panel shows the same image after the 4 QSO components have been subtracted, and from which it is possible to identify the presence of the deflector. Finally, the right-most panel shows the residuals after fitting and subtracting also the light of the lens galaxy. Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> reports the relative positions of all the QSO components obtained from the <em>r</em>-band DES images, as well as the inferred magnitudes for <em>g, r, i</em>, and <em>z</em> bands with their uncertainties, as calculated by <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span>.</p>                        <a id=\"132876934\" scrollto-destination=\"132876934\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/485/4/10.1093_mnras_stz781/1/m_stz781fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611465186&amp;Signature=Bco0eYtdzBzgaqjAB4-yKNFZhqkdpRrh-Aa4jq0JXeHCZp2yKUopK057rm57cNjuN6v1Qitgn0rNrC1iYhTJWauunHkkS68FsAcSqTbm4OcNCxMDoL4SCPrDHL~itQPS4E2d-Gv0fFmQSwxMcrsRHnsbLAWPzFYkN~Mfu7Cv7Xg~9lsDhtGMoXjR-i0j4S52ueDoGgUY2DDOpGkXBLf1GuF66sBxFpHOOoo45o-dyT-4cTkNy7fEt2TV4B17PMYD10vLugCy0ABDzwl7sVfZZHxo198QpgQpjvuH3J2DBAbSAyjaWREFkniaPFkeHmulX4dVBugZGwWp~678lbq5MA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Cut-outs generated combining g-, r-, i- and z-band DES images (upper panels) and Pan-STARRS images (middle panels) for WG0214-2105, and for WG2100-4452, observed only from DES (lower panels).        </a></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=132876936 id=\"132876936\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-1>4.1 Variability evidence for WG0214</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Quasar microlensing occurs when the light of the source, already deflected by the lens gravitational field, is also affected by the gravitational field of relatively low-mass (10<sup>\u22126</sup> &lt; <em>m</em>/M<sub>\u2299</sub> &lt; 10<sup>3</sup>) bodies moving along the line of sight (e.g. single stars, brown dwarfs, planets, globular clusters, etc.). More specifically, microlensing is observed when the angular size of such bodies is smaller than the Einstein radius (\u03b8) of the lensing system and therefore comparable with quasar angular size. Thus, microlensing is a very useful tool to constrain quasar structure as well to estimate the masses of these compact bodies (Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">During a microlensing event, the mass of the micro-deflector is not large enough to cause a measurable displacement of the light path, but, due to the relative motion between the source quasars, the lenses and the observer, a change in the magnification with time can be detected (Schmidt\u00a0&amp; Wambsganss <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib60\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib60\" data-open=\"bib60\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>). Thus, the apparent brightness of the source can change by more than a magnitude on time scales of weeks to months or years.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn6\" data-open=\"fn6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">6</a></sup> Unlike the intrinsic quasar variability, however, microlensing variability is uncorrelated between images.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Microlensing has a number of very important astrophysical applications. In particular, it can help in determining the existence and effects of compact objects along the line of sight, in studying in great detail the size, structure, and light distribution of the source quasars (Dai et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Morgan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; O\u2019Dowd et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) and in constraining the masses and mass distributions of lensing objects and their environments (e.g. Cowley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">For WG0214-2105, we can compare two magnitude measurements obtained from multiband images taken at different epochs: DES, taken in 2016, and Pan-STARRS, taken in 2014. Although with only two measurements one cannot build a detailed light curve, these data allowed us to detect time variation of the flux of each quasar component, which appears to be uncorrelated with wavelength and thus suggestive of a microlensing origin. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> plots the magnitudes calculated for different filter bands (<em>g, r, i</em>) from Pan-STARRS (upper panel) and DES (lower panel) for the four QSO images of WG0214-2105. We excluded the <em>z</em>-band image because it was very noisy for the Pan-STARRS case. The brightness of the B, C, and D components changes with time, without any clear correlation between wavelength and magnitude. This result seems to indicate a microlensing effect, although we stress that chromatic variability cannot be entirely excluded based on just two epochs of broad-band imaging. Another argument in favour of microlensing comes from Palanque-Delabrouille et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) and in particular from their Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>, which shows the variability structure function for a typical quasar (the change in amplitude as a function of time between observations at different epochs). The function predicts that a change of \u223c0.3\u22120.5 mag, similar to what we observe for the D component, is expected only if the two epochs are separated by several years.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn7\" data-open=\"fn7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">7</a></sup> We caution the reader, however, that delay among different light-curves might cause a large flux variation, as shown in Courbin et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) for the lens D0408. Flux ratio variations among light-curves also have implications for claims of substructure detection, as was shown explicitly by Agnello et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) on the same lens.</p>                        <a id=\"132876941\" scrollto-destination=\"132876941\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/485/4/10.1093_mnras_stz781/1/m_stz781fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611465186&amp;Signature=a56xu-T91Mvd94LS54taaQ5vqQ9F2izFg0RSSRhWu2yAh9pIo314vy30iAlZxjCiIyO99eg4oRJgJXLZv4Ywksf34TmtBuR1l6PuzGHcKGg8nXMAydP9hjhgVvsp~Gt95xy2OCh3QmYtX9EVzeQ278DgHNkn5v2rSYwytB4o76dsKdhTa7BE1ANb5IucyuXY5S~QFd-ni6j3YQPI3CUjdT0dsJZc45NGmz7LLgdmM7acMd7jN1BO~HrgwmWAkPZ1tlocN~pZ7ZipNVGpClBvOECv4R4ViNYrPmHInmFhP9wAfx8TCvPQ-hJ8or4sPSu5O5QMOQRdk7t2M8ME6b60Bw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Estimated magnitudes at different filter bands (g, r, i) from Pan-STARRS images taken in 2014 (upper panel) and from DES images taken in 2016 (lower panel) for the four QSO images of WG0214-2105. This result could indicate the presence of microlensing.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=132876942 id=\"132876942\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 SALT SPECTROSCOPIC FOLLOW-UP</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In 2018 November, we obtained long-slit spectroscopy for the two quadruplets with the Robert Stobie Spectrograph (RSS) instrument and the PG0900 grating (grating-angle \u00a0=\u00a015.875), covering from 4490 to 7540 \u00c5\u2009 with resolution <em>R</em>\u00a0= 1000 measured from the OI5577 sky line, and using a 2\u00a0\u00d7\u00a04 binning, corresponding to \u223c0.5 arcsec pix<sup>\u2212</sup><sup>1</sup> in the spatial direction and to 0.97\u00c5\u2009pix<sup>\u22121</sup> in the dispersion direction.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As already highlighted, these two DES systems, being bright and visible at the beginning of the SALT observation semester, have been used as \u2018test-cases\u2019 in modest observing condition (seeing &gt; 1.5 arcsec) and non-optimal observing time (twilight), mainly to test our choices of grating, spatial binning and integration time on target.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The data were reduced with two independent methods, namely the SALT science pipeline (<span class=\"small-caps\">pysalt</span>; Crawford et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>)<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn8\" data-open=\"fn8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">8</a></sup> and standard <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span> routines. One-dimensional (1D) spectra were extracted and analysed with custom <span class=\"small-caps\">idl</span> and <span class=\"small-caps\">mathematica</span> codes. In the following section we discuss the extraction of the spectra, de-blending of the components and estimation of the redshift for each target separately. The redshifts are reported in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"132876946\" scrollto-destination=\"132876946\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl3\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl3\" data-id=\"tbl3\"><span class=\"label\">Table 3.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Inferred redshifts for the lenses and the sources.          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/132876946\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=132876947 id=\"132876947\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-1>5.1 WG0214-2105</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We observed WG0214-2105 in two separate observing blocks with a slit of 1.5 arcsec\u00a0\u00d7 8 arcsec and two different position angles (PA): \u221235\u00b0 (PA\u221235 configuration) and +50\u00b0 (PA+50 configuration). Both observations were centred on the deflector, and both integrated for 1800 seconds on target. Seeing was not ideal (\u22481.8 arcsec) but the night was clear. These configurations were motivated by the need to maximize the exposure time on the faint lens galaxy, and simultaneously obtain at least two completely independent spectra of the QSO components (A+B+D from PA\u221235 and A+C from PA+50).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The extracted spectra for the two position angles are shown in the upper panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>, where we label the main quasar emission lines (Ly\u2009\u03b1, Si\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>], He\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]) that allowed a secure determination of the redshift of the source (<em>z<sub>s</sub></em>\u00a0= 3.229\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.004). This value is in good agreement (within 2\u03c3 error) with the value of <em>z<sub>s</sub></em>\u00a0= 3.242\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.005 reported in Lee (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>).</p>                        <a id=\"132876950\" scrollto-destination=\"132876950\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/485/4/10.1093_mnras_stz781/1/m_stz781fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611465186&amp;Signature=0fynBJqyNKV9wXAJ9bSxZoHAHxU7doC9I1nA1aPf5ET0YKg1kR0N17DMRXWjanzGWmChHAaDu5xL3uQeTItcYJQMeHQhe9qlM~kE2aCdu-P2ahQAo-kUDxynOfqIz5JTLB1DlpgzNdOctTIjMv-MgU1INwAlYYAeDVUYrCxTdIse5k3zvdFM3THZCamvGYPtppnmAQELUzpSakBTFoJYx1G3-yplP4ru-LFWLGp7qa6xXllEYaEuCknMxgbnkFSct74-IJyUH1r-2F9oMa5RLJknAuaLOaHzbT8pzNH8fMi-OQouduwq3kHCRPFoV1GlFct9N5dOyeRkT9CRBXQO3g__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"SALT spectra of the lensed quasar (upper panels) and redshift distribution of the deflector (lower panel) for WG0214-2105. We zoom-in on the most prominent emission lines (Ly\u2009\u03b1 in the left-hand panel, Si\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>+O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>] in the middle panel and He\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] in the right-hand panel) that allowed us to securely infer its redshift. We plot here the histogram of the spectroscopic redshifts from SDSS-DR14 <span class=\"monospace\">SpecPhotoAll</span> galaxies with similar Petrosian magnitudes (within 2\u03c3 uncertainties).</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Unfortunately the quality of the long-slit spectra and the high contamination by the quasar did not allow us to securely determine the redshift of the deflector (<em>z<sub>l</sub></em>), although we identified some absorption lines (corresponding to more than one redshift, and therefore indicating the presence of galaxies along the line of sight). Therefore we infer <em>z<sub>l</sub></em> from photometry. To estimate the photometric redshift of the deflector we compared its PSF colours as derived in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a> with galaxy spectra from the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS, DR14, Abolfathi et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). In particular, we select all galaxies in <span class=\"monospace\">SpecPhotoAll</span> with magnitudes within 2\u03c3 of those obtained from our photometry (we use the <span class=\"monospace\">petroMag</span> and its <span class=\"monospace\">petroMagErr</span> for each band) of the lens, and retain their spectroscopic redshifts. The resulting histogram, plotted in the lower panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>, is double peaked. We then calculated the mean and standard deviation of the both peaks, fitting two normal distributions: <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z_{l_1,WG0214}=0.22\\pm 0.09$|\u2060</span>, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z_{l_2,WG0214}=0.53\\pm 0.08$|\u2060</span>. We note that the second peak (higher) of the histogram is consistent with the tentative redshift reported in Lee (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>).</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=132876952 id=\"132876952\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-2>5.2 WG2100-4452</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">For WG2100-4452 we obtained only one slit position with PA = 40\u00b0 and width\u00a0=\u00a03.0 arcsec, observed under thin cloud and very high lunar brightness (94\u00a0per\u2009cent, corresponding to a moon distance of 30\u00b0). Unfortunately, with such a configuration, all four images of the QSO are blended in the slit; it is therefore impossible to properly separate the components, especially for the two brightest ones. For the dim C and D components, unfortunately the short integration time that we obtained (1200 s) did not allow us to identify their signal. However, having clear evidence for emission lines from A+B, given the very specific geometrical configuration and the colours, and finally, given that this system can be perfectly fit with a simple lens model (as we will show in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">6</a>), we are fully confident about its lensing nature.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The accurate astrometric information provided by our analysis helped us to decompose the two-dimensional (2D) spectrum, separating, at least partially, the lens from the source. To this end, we considered a two-component model, with the A+B QSO being the first and the deflector being the second. We estimated, directly from the DES images, that the separation between them is \u223c1.3 arcsec, which corresponds to roughly 2.5 binned pixels for our observing strategy. The 1D extracted spectra of the two components, source and lens, are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>. where we also highlight the emission and absorption lines we used to infer the spectroscopic redshifts (<em>z</em><sub><em>s,WG</em>2100</sub>\u00a0= 0.920\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.002 and <em>z</em><sub><em>l,WG</em>2100</sub>\u00a0= 0.203\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.002).</p>                        <a id=\"132876955\" scrollto-destination=\"132876955\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/485/4/10.1093_mnras_stz781/1/m_stz781fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611465186&amp;Signature=dIDjkVR8W6fEwXvLvsYc8hbyMpAHbGy9QoGvQ41oA0pCUcDSvBK5OCMmcYM3RwpvYdQ8lEDAp0EVXaENk22BU9kzAtC~83thAbzSbzgB~N3H4IDWml0gfNLijDGi2rtIhjhcWcVbaOKLuPuAAgvzDd5LZLpk-vRSu10hUusWSC6YROBKvLs-44ed~vPrA1bTtE9X3XMiQmEheBBHQH9a8nw9SNWjHtDhT6zueIC1fMIn6EUevM~y-~knxGbrcAVIigV2XRLNeO3QLm~s6vTMHhPYE-1lzj9WA8lQi8uAC~mb5R-W8w6ouvv8whKkzBOLe2ogXLGG0Ec3Tcmq-7wZMg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"SALT spectra of the lensed quasar (upper panel) and the deflector (lower panel) of WG2100-4452 smoothed with a boxcar of 5 pixels for better visualization. De-blending the multiple images of the QSO is unfortunately not possible with the current slit configuration.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stz781fig4.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/132876955/stz781fig4.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stz781fig4.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"132876955\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/485/4/10.1093_mnras_stz781/1/stz781fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611465186&Signature=dIm-C7AVML1qD9h1IH9qP~Zi9Z~qkHdYbCDMFsqZyUkQiYsCbD85wogU-SWoiun20SXzr4ocg3SXs7PkIaLdRi-GJh7AJK9BaPgOUoP-S0nMbKxJK9PEHdu179hgJfc3bzOmJZTqUYX6WL4OYpdxlb7xmY1dqG4n-jcdbA16KVuADqLuZbyuYQUVblt1V1T3BpscEG50dtHTZCTUlqDodqJRSE3FzZdpbyO5zOeZ3UQWfEcaAnNlotTSkjdR2jU1kn1igjol98pdkUPMt~YRKnHwke4TkRw0AgXHYVUZRooI3Efiafs1RkrDPQkd-0VjQRQ46P87IxcEnFG03LTYzg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=132876955&ar=5382053&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stz781fig4.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">SALT spectra of the lensed quasar (upper panel) and the deflector (lower panel) of WG2100-4452 smoothed with a boxcar of 5 pixels for better visualization. We securely infer the redshift for both the source and the deflector, thanks to the identification of emission and absorption lines, marked in the figure with vertical lines. De-blending the multiple images of the QSO is unfortunately not possible with the current slit configuration.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Using the Penalized Pixel Fitting (<span class=\"small-caps\">ppxf</span>) code of Cappellari (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), we extracted the stellar velocity dispersion of the deflector from its absorption-line spectrum, using a maximum penalized likelihood approach. The spectrum has been extracted along an aperture of 3 pixels (corresponding to an aperture of roughly 1.5 arcsec), after subtracting the emission from the source (the broad MgII line at \u03bb \u223c 5190 \u00c5 observed wavelength). As stellar templates for the fit, we selected 100 stars (F, G, K, M) from the MILES stellar template library of S\u00e1nchez-Bl\u00e1zquez et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib56\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib56\" data-open=\"bib56\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>), which cover the wavelength range 3525\u20137500 \u00c5 at 2.5 \u00c5 FWHM spectral resolution. The resulting fit, yielding a \u03c3<sub>\u22c6</sub>\u00a0= 287\u00a0\u00b1\u00a040\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>, is shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>. The statistical uncertainty (\u03b4\u03c3<sub><em>stat</em></sub>\u00a0= 38\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>) and the systematic uncertainty (\u03b4\u03c3<sub><em>sys</em></sub>\u00a0= 14\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup> due to the templates used, the region of the spectrum that we fitted, and the eighth order of multiplicative polynomial that we used to take care of the continuum) are added in quadrature.</p>                        <a id=\"132876957\" scrollto-destination=\"132876957\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/485/4/10.1093_mnras_stz781/1/m_stz781fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611465186&amp;Signature=NJApjGxL4evRulglvLf2V8hgNbLJ5qG8b5wrRZwOerpuX2xibVzisJ5CoFoQcdnSMwtnjHna6VaGLqbjBTVZiLBvkaOyrSYwXsd4ty5-sAbFQMkIKte9FX9UpJLXU64mTGaDatX7eSSmF4lymkwKBDeDVwjy4GrGTm8FAK5kXfuFxVnYHjHGiMW4mSFceHBXDOcTK9qY5iB0EzO5bRR~mZ73pSoH~Xh4VC8usfqBvR32HrtWf7dA4Td5GQYA~YngW~DlNUn1ykScv4Tu~aRy8U2N6y0JnaEIDvIXsAoyT9ll7ENMnuBaMiPKtxls79LFFgyI-t7F-Q~afEdKGVCEfA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"ppxf fit of the lens galaxy in WGA2100-4452 plotted in rest-frame wavelength and in normalized count units. The galaxy spectrum is showed in black and the best-fitting stellar template is overplotted in red. The galaxy spectrum is showed in black and the best-fitting stellar template is overplotted in red. Residuals of the fit are shown in light green while blue regions are those excluded from the fit.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stz781fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/132876957/stz781fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stz781fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"132876957\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/485/4/10.1093_mnras_stz781/1/stz781fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611465186&Signature=fVBONo6hy-PTqAgqtr1ijjfpoLPpgJFwvwy75oy6gkN5eZm0h1GBkSi6gOyiodhk86OK4Ycqzh6h6KjdFTGZ6YUe6f5pzKLPd4iZ281-jA6D~jxRi0S8RdPgTrYpdo7eq5nYRcUK14NkwOulDi~1tnGgSq7FQGOiPJO2jW03diusB7KH4PBt-LpgnyyjCZIch2wR3MqDLkwrFNiwiRDzmbMTIbcXZW2rK~G7-IhX6BxPeBCYDEUu~zIaEj4kXA92h~wVr8XAlZMQT~F-d8nnPn7ltyRw4mHpEzd0-I1WGUox0v58diJLQxYQVqMIcSb2Sd1DrsjGvYT-LAxc7p7vDQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=132876957&ar=5382053&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stz781fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"small-caps\">ppxf</span> fit of the lens galaxy in WGA2100-4452 plotted in rest-frame wavelength and in normalized count units. The galaxy spectrum is showed in black and the best-fitting stellar template is overplotted in red. Residuals of the fit are shown in light green while blue regions are those excluded from the fit.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=132876958 id=\"132876958\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6>6 LENS MODELS</h2>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">To model the two quadruplets, we made use of the publicly available software <span class=\"small-caps\">glafic</span>, presented in Oguri (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib44\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib44\" data-open=\"bib44\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>). The code allows one to efficiently fit lensed images for both point-like and extended sources, also handling multiple sources, and considering a wide range of lens potentials. We tested two different models to estimate the parameters: first, a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE) mass model, and second a power density ellipsoid (PDE) model where the mass density slope is left as free parameter. The SIE is one of the most frequently used lens model for strong gravitational lenses since it describes a mass distribution with a flat rotation curve. The convergence of the model is <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"update222119_equ1\" content-id=\"update222119_equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\n\\kappa =\\frac{b_{SIE}(q)}{2\\sqrt{\\tilde{x}^2+\\tilde{y}^2/q^2}} ,\r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div>where <em>q</em>\u00a0= 1 \u2212 <em>e</em> is the axial ratio (with <em>e</em> being the ellipticity), and the coordinates <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\tilde{x},\\tilde{y}$|</span> are rotated by the position angle <em>PA<sub>SIE</sub></em>, defined east of north and assuming that the positive direction is north. The normalization factor <em>b<sub>SIE</sub></em>(<em>q</em>), for a spherical case (<em>q</em>\u00a0= 1), agrees with the Einstein radius (\u03b8<sub><em>SIE</em></sub>) and is related to the galaxy velocity dispersion (\u03c3<sub><em>SIE</em></sub>) as: <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"update222119_equ2\" content-id=\"update222119_equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\nb_{SIE}(q=1)= \\theta _{SIE} = 4\\pi \\left(\\frac{\\sigma _{SIE}}{c}\\right)^2\\frac{D_{ls}}{D_s} ,\r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>where <em>D<sub>s</sub></em> is the angular diameter distance of the source from the observer and <em>D<sub>ls</sub></em> is the relative distance between the lens and the source.</div><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">The PDE model is more useful than the SIE model for studying the effect of the radial density slope on lensing. The convergence, defined in Keeton (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>), is <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"update222119_equ3\" content-id=\"update222119_equ3\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\n\\kappa =\\frac{3-\\beta }{2} (\\theta _{PDE})^{1-\\beta }\\left(\\tilde{x}^2+\\tilde{y}^2/q^2\\right)^{(1-\\beta)/2} ,\r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(3)</span></div>where \u03b8<sub><em>PDE</em></sub> is the Einstein radius. The PDE model corresponds to an isothermal model for \u03b2\u00a0= 2.</div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The SIE model has seven free parameters: <em>x</em> and <em>y</em> coordinates of the galaxy and of the source (true position), ellipticity, position angle, and velocity dispersion. The PDE has eight free parameters: Einstein radius, <em>x</em> and <em>y</em> coordinates of the galaxy and of the source, ellipticity, position angle, and mass density slope. Since from the DES images and photometric analysis we have eight constraints for each system (<em>x,y</em>, apparent positions of the four multiple images), both models are fully constrained.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We used the inferred spectroscopic redshifts for the sources (<em>z</em><sub><em>s,WG</em>0214</sub>\u00a0= 3.229, <em>z</em><sub><em>s,WG</em>2100</sub>\u00a0= 0.92). For the deflector redshifts, we used the spectroscopic value obtained for WG2100-4452 (<em>z</em><sub><em>l,WG</em>2100</sub>\u00a0= 0.203) and the photometric ones for WG0214-2105 (we run the model twice, one time assuming <em>z</em><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$_{l_1, WG0214} = 0.22\\pm 0.09$|\u2060</span>, and the second time assuming <em>z</em><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$_{l_2, WG0214} = 0.53\\pm 0.08$|\u2060</span>). The model results are reported in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl4\" data-open=\"tbl4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>, where we also report reduced chi-square (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\chi ^{2}_{\\nu }$|\u2060</span>) values to provide a quantitative measure of the goodness of the fit. Overall a good agreement between the two models is found. For the PDE model, the best fit mass density slopes we recovered are \u03b2<sub><em>WG</em>0214</sub>\u00a0= 2.1\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2 and \u03b2<sub><em>WG</em>2100</sub>\u00a0= 1.9\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2, both consistent with an isothermal profile.</p>                        <a id=\"132876963\" scrollto-destination=\"132876963\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl4\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl4\" data-id=\"tbl4\"><span class=\"label\">Table 4.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Model parameters obtained for the two quadruplets: ellipticity, position angle, and Einstein radius from both models; mass density slope from PDE and galaxy velocity dispersion and masses within the Einstein radius from SIE. We also report, for each model and each system, the modest value of the \u03c7<sup>2</sup> divided by the degrees of freedom to judge the quality of the fit. For WG0214-2105, we report model parameters obtained assuming <em>z</em><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$_{l_1} = 0.22\\pm 0.09$|</span> in the first line of the table, and assuming <em>z</em><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$_{l_2} = 0.53\\pm 0.08$|</span> in the second line of the table.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th>ID<span        </a></div></div></div><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">For the SIE model, with the velocity dispersion derived by <span class=\"small-caps\">glafic</span> for each deflector redshift, we obtained and estimate of the Einstein radius from equation\u00a0(<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-update222119_equ2\"></span><a href=\"#update222119_equ2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>), and an estimate of the deflectors\u2019 masses inside the Einstein radii using the following equation: <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"update222119_equ4\" content-id=\"update222119_equ4\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\nM_{Ein} = \\theta _{SIE}^{2}\\dfrac{c^2D_{l}D_{s}}{4GD_{ls}} ,\r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(4)</span></div>where <em>D<sub>l</sub></em> is the distance of the lens from the observer and <em>c</em> is the speed of light. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a> shows the mass models for WG0214-2105 (left-hand panel) and WG2100-4452 (right-hand panel) in the SIE case. We plot caustics and critical curves, as well as the apparent and true positions of the sources. We note that the flux ratios could be strongly perturbed by microlensing effects. Therefore, the magnitude difference of the quasar images has been excluded from the model.</div>                        <a id=\"132876965\" scrollto-destination=\"132876965\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig6\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 6.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/485/4/10.1093_mnras_stz781/1/m_stz781fig6.jpeg?Expires=1611465186&amp;Signature=c464NKftYKbbJYBCqFccVzqUHOWyT9Gb2DGOFlLaLran3Djv94fpTDIYcgqsdUeGOYoVuvD0IYAdbtfBhDtgLv5eMQyrPWBIkFaVgIoMTvPsU7~Fe9VNRFZG3jOJGhNrapL6t1sj47MWJEKGQCL3~VaWFeT8XhyevoOnAiVpiQdflyWF7yHG5jaNYiZqZ4f2-XypRAAevZPr8uXLXgWo5VmVq9l3FyT-WcypLuT13LdAOqVQhL4qalZGejH1HOEp-8VNVQGfrbGXxdxQPd0EDZtSLAKPSexhHydZG7TDf7~CGLXzBsr74tiYJjCULU9YcHz2~eVul72IGutHOD7igA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Mass model fit obtained assuming an SIE profile matter distribution for WG0214-2105 (left-hand panel) and WG2100-4452 (right-hand panel). The QSO components are labelled following the same convention adopted in Fig.\u00a01.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stz781fig6.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/132876965/stz781fig6.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stz781fig6.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"132876965\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/485/4/10.1093_mnras_stz781/1/stz781fig6.jpeg?Expires=1611465186&Signature=r7rJ3vkQpXQA2ZG2t25Fp-hh66QqBhrN5llaKnFaXrfzR1gLaVWRqmojA2XIk7-rv4AJ72eWE9090eqOuy4oGpwkMX~33leSUQgEJo4j40TIeIJjBaxJ3nx-jmeHlmwT8aluR~D~zam9S9dkYgMxCr2mcsULfJgHOo6~Q8HMUApqMOZ3LuPJYa4mtcrJwkYyF8tplnFn0dcD3Tk--G1dM4mBGkS-lzgxFAKAaeSVMJuuZ8GEexGvsA-EJaW5TpVUIZ9~2h4I5WXPCBcYkOX2zjsLgjOGEf3m2Wed5Sem9nOlcAYqOyaV~LJpxTn3H~VekF3hZwW7bJwjCCmJ7uqXig__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=132876965&ar=5382053&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stz781fig6.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Mass model fit obtained assuming an SIE profile matter distribution for WG0214-2105 (left-hand panel) and WG2100-4452 (right-hand panel). The red and blue curves correspond to the critical curves and caustics of the model, respectively. The black circles with internal crosses show the observed positions inferred from the DES images, the orange filled circles show the predicted image positions, and finally the green filled circle indicates the calculated true source position for each system. The QSO components are labelled following the same convention adopted in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Finally, we calculated the magnification and time-delay values for all components, relative to the brightest one (A), and report the results in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl5\" data-open=\"tbl5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> for both models. Unfortunately the code does not allow one to estimate the errors on time delays and magnitudes. We have therefore written a small python script to calculate them using a Markov-Chain Monte Carlo approach. We generated 100\u2009000 models and obtained a normal distribution for each of the estimated parameters, computing, then, the mean and standard deviation values.</p>                        <a id=\"132876967\" scrollto-destination=\"132876967\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl5\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl5\" data-id=\"tbl5\"><span class=\"label\">Table 5.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Quasar image parameters for the best fits obtained for the two models we tested: an SIE mass model and a PDE model. Component A is taken as reference. no-formula-id\">\u2060|$z_{l_1,WG0214}=0.22\\pm 0.09$|\u2060</span>, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z_{l_2,WG0214}=0.53\\pm 0.08$|\u2060</span>) separated by commas.</p></div> style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th></tr><tr><th><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>(arcmin)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>(arcmin)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>(mag)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>(mag)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>(d)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>(d)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>WG0214-2105\u00a0</td><td>A\u00a0</td><td>0.00\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>0.00\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05\u00a0</td><td>\u22610\u00a0</td><td>\u22610\u00a0</td><td>\u22610\u00a0</td><td>\u22610\u00a0</td><td>\u22610\u00a0</td><td>\u22610\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>WG0214-2105\u00a0</td><td>B\u00a0</td><td>0.46\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.91\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u00a0</td><td>0.7\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1\u00a0</td><td>0.7\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2\u00a0</td><td>0.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.3\u00a0</td><td>1.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.8\u00a0</td><td>3.5\u00a0\u00b1\u00a01.0\u00a0</td><td>3.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a01.6\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>WG0214-2105\u00a0</td><td>C\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.84\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04\u00a0</td><td>\u22121.69\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05\u00a0</td><td>0.7\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1\u00a0</td><td>0.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2\u00a0</td><td>\u22124.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a01.5\u00a0</td><td>\u22124.1\u00a0\u00b1\u00a03.3\u00a0</td><td>\u221212.5\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02.9\u00a0</td><td>\u221211.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a07.3\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>WG0214-2105\u00a0</td><td>D\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.90\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.06\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.18\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04\u00a0</td><td>0.6\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1\u00a0</td><td>0.6\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1\u00a0</td><td>1.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.3\u00a0</td><td>0.9\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.5\u00a0</td><td>2.5\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.8\u00a0</td><td>2.5\u00a0\u00b1\u00a01.6\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Name\u00a0</td><td>Comp.\u00a0</td><td>\u03b4x\u00a0</td><td>\u03b4y\u00a0</td><td>\u0394<em>mag<sub>SIE</sub></em>\u00a0</td><td>\u0394<em>mag<sub>PDE</sub></em>\u00a0</td><td>\u0394<em>t<sub>SIE</sub></em>\u00a0</td><td>\u0394<em>t<sub>PDE</sub></em>\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td><td>(arcmin)\u00a0</td><td>(arcmin)\u00a0</td><td>(mag)\u00a0</td><td>(mag)\u00a0</td><td>(d)\u00a0</td><td>(d)\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>WG2100-4452\u00a0</td><td>A\u00a0< /td><td>0.00\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>0.00\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u00a0</td><td>\u22610\u00a0</td><td>\u22610\u00a0</td><td>\u22610\u00a0</td><td>\u22610\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>WG2100-4452\u00a0</td><td>B\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.44\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.33\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u00a0</td><td>0.12\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td><td>0.08\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.12\u00a0</td><td>0.15\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td><td>0.14\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.08\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>WG2100-4452\u00a0</td><td>C\u00a0</td><td>\u22122.48\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td><td>0.35\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u00a0</td><td>1.29\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05\u00a0</td><td>\u22121.37\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.13\u00a0</td><td>\u22129.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a01.6\u00a0</td><td>\u22129.0\u00a0\u00b1\u00a04.3\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>WG2100-4452\u00a0</td><td>D\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.85\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>1.89\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04\u00a0</td><td>2.0\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1\u00a0</td><td>\u22121.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2\u00a0</td><td>11.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02.7\u00a0</td><td>10.4\u00a0\u00b1\u00a04.0\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/132876967\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">We caution the reader that microlensing can influence time-delay measurements, making them time variable. This is due, as described in Tie\u00a0&amp; Kochanek (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib73\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib73\" data-open=\"bib73\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), to a combination of two effects. First, the quasar disc has an inclination with respect to the line-of-sight, and thus different parts of the disc lie at different projected distances to the source. This configuration can change time delays on the scale of the light crossing time of the accretion disc (typically of the order of light days). Secondly, microlensing can cause a differential magnification of the temperature of the emission from the disc, causing a differential time delay on the scale of the light crossing time.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The results (expressed in changes of magnitudes and time delays with respect to the brightest component) obtained with the two different models agree with each other within 1\u03c3 errors. As expected, the SIE model produces smaller errors on all quantities, having less free parameters. Moreover, we note that the time delays highly depend on the deflector redshift: increasing the galaxy redshift, the time-delay values increase proportionally.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The relative positions inferred from the lensing model and directly calculated from the images (in <em>r</em> band), always with respect to the brightest QSO component (A), agree perfectly with each other. This is also clearly visible from Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>, where we report with orange filled circles the model predicted positions and with empty black circled crosses the positions directly obtained from the DES images.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=132876971 id=\"132876971\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec7>7 CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper, we have presented the spectroscopic confirmation and lens modelling of two new quadruply lensed quasars recently found in the DES public footprints, namely WG0214-2105 and WG2100-4452. The quadruplets were both found with a method based on three main steps: an infrared (WISE) colour-pre-selection of QSO-like objects, a morphological criterion based on multiple matches in the <em>Gaia</em> DR2 catalogue and finally, visual inspection of the outcomes. We refer the reader to <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a> for a detailed description of the search methodology and to <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">ARN18</a> for the discovery reports.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Since the only missing ingredient to unambiguously confirm the lensing nature of these objects, whose geometrical configuration and chromaticity are typical of lensed QSOs, was spectroscopy, we targeted them with the Southern African Large Telescope. For both systems, we calculated the redshifts of the deflectors and the sources, confirming their multiple lensing nature. We obtained z<sub><em>s</em></sub>\u00a0= 3.229\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.004 for WG0214-2105 thanks to the identification of the strong Ly\u2009\u03b1 line and other weaker lines such as Si\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>], He\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]. We inferred instead <em>z<sub>s</sub></em>\u00a0= 0.920\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.002 for WG2100-4452, thanks to the identification of the prominent Mg\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> emission line. Only for WG2100-4452 we could estimate the deflector redshift (<em>z<sub>l</sub></em>\u00a0= 0.203\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.002) directly from the spectral absorption lines (i.e. CaK, CaH, G4300, H\u2009\u03b2, Mgb, NaD), since the galaxy is quite bright (<em>r</em>\u00a0= 17.68\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01 mag, see Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>). For the other lens, we infer the redshift of the source using optical magnitudes that we obtained performing DIA and photometry (presented in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Microlensing studies require multiple images of a system taken in different epochs. We presented here preliminary evidence of time variability for one of the two systems, WG0214-2105, obtained measuring the photometry of all the components from DES (taken in 2016) and Pan-STARRS (taken in 2014). A change of \u22480.4 mag is visible for the faintest QSO component (D), and other two components show smaller changes too. Although with only two epochs separated by 2 yr, intrinsic chromatic variability cannot be excluded, we argue in favour of microlensing because we do not see any clear correlation with wavelength. Moreover, the lens model inferred time delays are of the order of a few days and the probability that a quasar changes its magnitude by \u2248 half a magnitude in such a short time is very low. We also note that, as shown in Schechter\u00a0&amp; Wambsganss (2002), microlensing in saddle-points (B, D) is more likely in the presence of a smoothly distributed (dark matter) component.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Finally, we confirmed the work of Wynne\u00a0&amp; Schechter (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib81\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib81\" data-open=\"bib81\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), finding that these systems are perfectly compatible with simple lens models. We tested two different lens models, specifically an SIE approximation where the mass density slope is fixed but the stellar velocity dispersion is allowed to vary, and a PDE model where the Einstein radius and the mass density slope are free parameters. For both models, we constrained the <em>x</em> and <em>y</em> positions of the source and the deflector, the ellipticity and the position angle. We finally obtained for both quadruplets changes in magnitudes and time-delay measurements for each of the quasar multiple image, finding that, overall, these quantities do not depend much on the chosen model.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To conclude, we demonstrated that the planned integration times (set by the magnitudes and colours of the sources in the photometric survey catalogues) are long enough to obtain SALT spectra with sufficient signal-to-noise ratios to detect emission lines from the QSOs and, in most of the cases, also absorption lines from the lens. Our observing strategy works properly and will allow us, once the programme will be completed, to confirm many among the \u223c300 lens candidates (arcs and QSOs) that we selected in the last 2 yr from the KIDS and KABS surveys.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=132876977 id=\"132876977\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" data-legacy-id=ack1>ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">CS has received funding from the European Union\u2019s Horizon 2020 research and innovation programme under the Marie Sk\u0142odowska-Curie actions grant agreement no. 664931. NRN acknowledges financial support from the European Union\u2019s Horizon 2020 research and innovation programme under the Marie Sk\u0142odowska-Curie grant agreement no. 721463 to the SUNDIAL ITN network.
